<user_id>101639272871426856304< /user_id>< name>
Mike Hua</name>
< time>
1526452020243<//time>
< rating>
2</rating>
< review>
I was in town looking for a Chinese lunch spot. Upon arrival, the wait was conspicuously long, but decided to wait because the soup dumplings looked really appetizing. When getting seated after 30 minutes, I realized that the restaurant was severely understaffed not only outside the kitchen but also inside as well for a Sunday noon service. Long story short, we put order in for 4 dishes but only ate 2 because they simply couldn't turn around the remaining 2 dishes within 20 minutes of serving the first two. The waiter was nice enough to explain the under-staffing situation, but assessing the situation at the time, we suspected even another 20 minutes wouldn't be enough.

On to the review of the dishes. The soup dumplings were actually not bad. I could tell they were freshly made and the dough skins were made very thin and chewy, just the way I like them. The fillings were fairly soupy and the soup was light and flavorful, but not too oily. Although they executed this dish very well, I was heavily disappointed in the other two dishes. The smoke fish was one of the worst I've had because it was clear to me that the dish was made a while ago - too cold even for a cold dish - and the execution was rather poor. The fish tasted extremely bland even when I smothered them in sauce. I always enjoyed eating this dish growing up because the father-side of my family always prepared this dish. It really bothered me that they completely butchered this dish. Finally, the soy milk with Chinese You-Tiao is at best mediocre because they've managed over-soak the You-Tiao to the point it was falling apart. All in all, if I were to return again, probably will just stick to the safe dishes like the soup dumplings.< /review>

<user_name>Thomas Perez< /user_name><rating>5< /rating></record></dataset><record>
<user>115014077999082450395< /user><username>Cecilia Knapp<//username>< Date>
1577685477801< /Date>
<rate>3<//rate>< Review>
It's just ok, I've definitely had better dumplings at other places. My friend, who is vegetarian, brought me, my brother, and nephew here to try. She said her non-vegetarian friend really liked it and she at least has some options. We had an order of the pork XLB, pork pan-fried dumplings, green onion pancake, vegetarian potstickers, and stir-fried rice cakes. These are all items I've had at other places and I was underwhelmed. The wrapper on the XLB were too thick, though our order did come out nice and hot. There was a good amount of broth and the taste of the pork was good, the wrapper was just way too thick and doughy. Same with the pan-fried dumplings - they were almost as thick and doughy as steamed pork buns that you'd get a dim sum, but with the little pork meatball inside. The green onion pancakes were fried nice and golden and had a good taste, they just weren't flakey layers like I'm used to, but at least they were not oily. I didn't try the vegetarian potstickers but they did erroneously give us pork ones at first which my vegetarian friend found out after she bit into one. The rice cakes were ok, nothing extra special about them.

It was easy to find street parking and walk right in to get a table for 4 at 6:30 on a Sunday, but I don't know that I'm ever planning to go back.< /Review>

<Time>1457935253890</Time><Rate>4< /Rate><Text>Authentic Chinese food. Yummy dumplings!

Came by on a Sunday evening for dinner. There was a line outside the restaurant, we waited for approx 15mins before we were seated.

We were promptly served with tea and shortly after, a server came by to take our orders. We ordered Hot and Sour soup (3/5), Shanghai Dumplings (4/5), buns with condensed milk (4/5) and Beef with capsicum (3/5).

I had wanted to order their savory soy bean milk, unfortunately they are only available for breakfast/lunch.

The portions were huge for each of the dishes, enough for 3-4 to share. It was two of us so we ended up packing quite a bit of food home.

Overall, the food are authentic and tasty. Typical Chinese restaurants are really noisy, this was manageable.

Will be back again.<//Text>< pictures>

Arun Venkatesan< /name>
<date>1386377086403</date><rating>4</rating>< Review>
If you come here on the weekend or any other peak time, be ready to wait. We waited for 40 minutes for Sunday lunch.

The food here is definitely better than the average dumpling place. We had the soup dumplings (xiao long bao) and a few other varieties. The service was great. The owners and waiters treated us like children.

The decor and atmosphere is standard for true Chinese restaurants like this. Expect some hustle and bustle along with laughing, children playing, etc. Definitely the kind of place that could make you feel alive.

Come here with friends or family. You won't be disappointed.< /Review>

<gmapID>0x808f77a45cc3c221:0x1be4920351b20539<//gmapID><text>As a newcomer 3 years ago to "real" Chinese food (you other midwest transplants probably know what I'm talking about) I made it my quest to try xiao long bao (the steamed dumplings with pork & soup) at every Shanghainese restaurant that offered it.

My wife's is Cantonese and grew up in the bay area with a restaraunt loving family, so over the years I have collected a list of dumpling rating criteria.

The ratios are arguably the most important criteria  to me.  If there is too little soup, there is less flavor.  If the dumpling is too thick, it can mask the flavor.  If there is not enough pork...well you see where I'm going with this.

Other xiao long bao issues:
- Served in a tiny foil tin that almost invariably sticks to dumpling
- Very salty broth
- Tough and/or dense port

This is turning into a food theory post, so I'll get to the point.

The Shanghai Dumpling Shop consistently serves delicious Xiao Long Bao.  I know the ratios preference is matter of opinion and maybe you like really salty soup, but I think these are the BEST.

And, maybe the highest praise I can offer in our hyper-critical Bay Area dining market:  "I have never heard anyone say anything bad about these wonderful dumplings."</text><Response>None< /Response>< Pics>
None< /Pics>

<user_name>Nei Ng<//user_name><Pics>None< /Pics>< Gmap_id>
0x808f77a45cc3c221:0x1be4920351b20539< /Gmap_id>
<response>None</response>< Rating>
3<//Rating>
< Text>
I had dinner here with a few friends, and it wasn't bad. After a brief wait, we were seated inside, and our waitress was surprisingly nice. She was more warm and welcoming than what you'd expect from typical Chinese service. Our food came pretty fast, too. Yay.

Stir Fried Pea Sprouts with Garlic - I liked the strong garlic flavor, but some of the pea sprouts were stiff around the stalks. The flavor wasn't bad, but the quality could've been better.

Stir Fried Rice Cakes - Mushy. Some pieces kept sticking to my teeth, which was annoying. They tasted pretty savory, but some more wok hei would've been better. I should mention that I'm not a super big fan of rice cakes, so I'm a little biased here.

Shanghai Stir Fried Noodles - Pretty good. The noodles had a tender, smooth bite that I liked. They had a savory flavor like the rice cakes but with a more enjoyable texture.

XLB - The skins were thin and broke open smoothly. There was a healthy amount of broth inside, and it had a very slight bitterness that reminded me of ginseng. Although I liked that part, I still thought it could've been more aromatic. More ginger and green onions would've made the flavors pop out more. The texture of the pork stuffing was a little on the gritty side, too. Still, the XLB weren't bad, but I wouldn't go out of my way to come here.< /Text>

< text>
Recommend this place. You can find many traditional and common Chinese entrees here, including homestyle entrees and Chinese street food, e.g., sweet soy milk and Chinese donut. They also make great Chinese donuts and crab meat xiao long bao. Their food is authentic Chinese and overall well-made and delicious. However, as with many casual Chinese restaurants, there isn't much in terms of food presentation. The service is fast and friendly. In terms of decor and ambiance, this is not a hole-in the-wall joint, but the place needs updated chairs and renovation. Because of the delicious food, this place can get crowded, lending to a lively atmosphere. Overall a great and enjoyable eating experience lending a little bit of nostalgia for those of us who enjoyed Chinese street food growing up.< /text>
